mrs
ferrar at first reasonably endeavoured to dissuade he from marry miss dashwood by every argument in her power told he that in miss morton he would have a woman of high rank and large fortune and enforce the assertion by observe that miss morton be the daughter of a nobleman with thirty thousand pound while miss dashwood be only the daughter of a private gentleman with no more than three but when she find that though perfectly admit the truth of her representation he be by no mean incline to be guide by it she judge it wisest from the experience of the past to submit--and therefore after such an ungracious delay as she owe to her own dignity and as serve to prevent every suspicion of good-will she issue her decree of consent to the marriage of edward and elinor
what she would engage to do towards augment their income be next to be consider and here it plainly appear that though edward be now her only son he be by no mean she eld for while robert be inevitably endow with a thousand pound a-year not the small objection be make against edward s take order for the sake of two hundred and fifty at the utmost nor be anything promise either for the present or in future beyond the ten thousand pound which have be give with fanny

with an income quite sufficient to their want thus secure to they they have nothing to wait for after edward be in possession of the living but the readiness of the house to which colonel brandon with an eager desire for the accommodation of elinor be make considerable improvement and after wait some time for their completion after experience as usual a thousand disappointment and delay from the unaccountable dilatoriness of the workman elinor as usual break through the first positive resolution of not marry till every thing be ready and the ceremony take place in barton church early in the autumn
the first month after their marriage be spend with their friend at the mansion-house from whence they could superintend the progress of the parsonage and direct every thing as they like on the spot could chuse paper project shrubbery and invent a sweep

i will not say that i be disappointed my dear sister say john as they be walk together one morning before the gate of delaford house that would be say too much for certainly you have be one of the most fortunate young woman in the world as it be
but i confess it would give i great pleasure to call colonel brandon brother
his property here his place his house every thing be in such respectable and excellent condition and his woods i have not see such timber any where in dorsetshire as there be now stand in delaford hanger and though perhaps marianne may not seem exactly the person to attract he--yet i think it would altogether be advisable for you to have they now frequently stay with you for as colonel brandon seem a great deal at home nobody can tell what may happen--for when people be much throw together and see little of anybody else--and it will always be in your power to set she off to advantage and so forth in short you may as well give she a chance--you understand i but though mrs

the whole of lucy s behaviour in the affair and the prosperity which crown it therefore may be hold forth as a most encouraging instance of what an earnest an uncease attention to self-interest however its progress may be apparently obstruct will do in secure every advantage of fortune with no other sacrifice than that of time and conscience
when robert first seek her acquaintance and privately visit she in bartlett s building it be only with the view impute to he by his brother
he merely mean to persuade she to give up the engagement and as there could be nothing to overcome but the affection of both he naturally expect that one or two interview would settle the matter
in that point however and that only he erred for though lucy soon give he hope that his eloquence would convince she in time another visit another conversation be always want to produce this conviction

marianne dashwood be bear to an extraordinary fate
she be bear to discover the falsehood of her own opinion and to counteract by her conduct her most favourite maxim
she be bear to overcome an affection form so late in life as at seventeen and with no sentiment superior to strong esteem and lively friendship voluntarily to give her hand to another and that other a man who have suffer no less than herself under the event of a former attachment whom two year before she have consider too old to be married and who still seek the constitutional safeguard of a flannel waistcoat
but so it be
instead of fall a sacrifice to an irresistible passion as once she have fondly flatter herself with expecting instead of remain even for ever with her mother and find she only pleasure in retirement and study as afterwards in she more calm and sober judgment she have determine on she find herself at nineteen submit to new attachment enter on new duty place in a new home a wife the mistress of a family and the patroness of a village
colonel brandon be now as happy as all those who well love he believe he deserve to be in marianne he be console for every past affliction her regard and her society restore his mind to animation and his spirit to cheerfulness and that marianne find her own happiness in form his be equally the persuasion and delight of each observe friend
marianne could never love by half and her whole heart become in time as much devoted to her husband as it have once be to willoughby
willoughby could not hear of her marriage without a pang and his punishment be soon afterwards complete in the voluntary forgiveness of mrs
smith who by state his marriage with a woman of character as the source of her clemency give he reason for believe that have he behave with honour towards marianne he might at once have be happy and rich
that his repentance of misconduct which thus bring its own punishment be sincere need not be doubted nor that he long thought of colonel brandon with envy and of marianne with regret
but that he be for ever inconsolable that he flee from society or contract an habitual gloom of temper or die of a broken heart must not be depend on--for he do neither
he live to exert and frequently to enjoy himself
his wife be not always out of humour nor his home always uncomfortable and in his breed of horse and dog and in sporting of every kind he find no inconsiderable degree of domestic felicity
for marianne however--in spite of his incivility in survive her loss--he always retain that decide regard which interest he in every thing that befell she and make she his secret standard of perfection in woman and many a rise beauty would be slight by he in after-day as bear no comparison with mrs
